Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, either one or more, and they are old and consist of large amounts of cold, moist, corrupted humor, and they are treated as we have described in divisions, but it does not help, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is completely under the armpit, poking and poking in a triangular shape, and one cautery under the hip.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face swell, then on the face put .i. large cautery on the stomach, as it is before said, and .i. another on the liver, and i. another on the mouse all over the cautery clave; and let the cautery remain open for a long time. After cure the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnosity which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you scrape the thelul, heat the cautery which looks like  .i. razor, and then put it all ablaze on the scraped thelul; and keep your hand so that the cauteries come to the source of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or .ij., and if there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each one as we have said. After curing with profiting ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is a fistula, and it is suppurating and exuding pus and corrupted moisture, you should test it with a thin probe, and be careful to only go as far as the tent is inserted into the fistula. Then heat up the cautery like a razor and place it into the fistula according to how deep the tent went in, and repeat the cautery until the corrupt flesh is burned—once or twice or thrice, depending on the amount needed; be careful not to burn the nerves surrounding the area, and avoid the large veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestines, be careful of these areas as well, and do not apply the cautery directly to bone, and think that it is not feeling anything; after that, clean the wound until it heals completely, and if there is still pus coming out for a long time, know that the wound has been fully healed.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, and there are strong winds, and it does not go away, then you should cauterize the kidneys with a hot iron on both sides, as we have said before. If we cauterize in the middle, it will require three cauteries in a line, and they will be more effective.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic region begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the tip of a thumb; and he makes another cautery over the back, or two if you need it; and the cauteries should be curved as described before.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and does not conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore one should make three cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries over the back; and the cauteries should be curved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the socket of the hip joint, and due to this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and if the places of dislocation are discovered as hollow, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket with a .i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and the cautery should be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make .iij cauteries of the olive-sized great, and let the cautery be as deep as all the wounds; and heal it until it is better.
de la dolor de la hainche	of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the disease is cured with what we have said in the section on cures, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the disease of the gross humors with stinking pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, let him be cauterized; and the manner of cautery is according to two methods: one is with burning medicines, and the other is fire cautery. Fire cautery depends on many methods, among which one is to cautarize the hip joint in a triangular shape according to this form, and make a good depth and size, and let there be between each cauterization the thickness of a thumb, and the cauteries are olive-shaped; sometimes a cauterization is made in the middle over the head of the hip, so that there are four of them according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries where the pain is felt, and one above the ankle on the inside of the foot; and let the cautery be cuticular, and burn the thickness of the skin; and if the pain extends to one or both sides of the foot, cauterize where the pain is felt with three or four cauteries, using the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do it more; and if he feels the pain below the knee towards the thigh, do cauterization with a knife or circular cautery, and be careful with all your cauterizations that you don't leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I have seen several who had cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet as well, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the feet. After that, he received a stomach solution from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, do cauterization in one and the other, according to this manner. // And they said about the cautery of the hip, of which here is the way, make a piece of iron and let it be at the head as thick as a little finger, or a little less, and let it be pierced from one end to the other with holes spaced out the width of a finger joint; and let the holes be on both sides, and also like knots, and there is a handle of iron well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and dripping, and then put it on the box of the hip joint, and let it be turned to the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery and leave it for 3 days; and then make a plaster of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery sparingly because of its regard, and see little of those who employ it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries which can endure it, and where it occurs.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, whether from falling or impact or from excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter, none of these appearances are worth cauterizing for, except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has voided foul pills or other similar remedies, to make three lines marked with ink on the back, where the pain persists; and in each line, make 5 cauteries, or more according to the strength and amount that the patient can endure. The cauteries should be performed using the cautery instrument called "poins". If you see fit, make 3 or 4 cauteries with the medium-sized cautery instrument according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a stiff neck when they wake up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine in the back and in us the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you cure it, then cauterize it with a silver cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the purple cautery colors each part of the vertebrae evenly. And if you see [the vertebrae], cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery .ij or .iij lines wide, and have the points close to each other. After curing the area until it is healed according to what we have said, be careful not to apply cautery in gurbosity which is in the webbing of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moistors that spread throughout the body's members, and when pain comes in the feet, which they properly call 'podagra', and when it is caused by a cold condition and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cautery in the following way: make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is a need to prick the face of the foot, then do the cautery all around the point on the foot they call 'point'. And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then do cautery on each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries of each part, using only olive oil cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but hold your hand no harder than until the thickness of the skin is burnt.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, then administer the cautery we described in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then prick around the wrist 2 lines; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, then prick each joint and the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbow or up to the shoulder, then cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give medicines. For if you take good care of him and purge the flux, then he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the jaw
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a hernia occurs in the groin, and the testicles descend into the scrotum, this is new, so when you see it being cured, he must not eat that day. He should use things that loosen the belly so that the feces can exit his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to hold his breath until the testicles are healed, and bring them up to your fingers, and sign underneath the hernia on the bone of the groin, and all around a sign that looks like half a circle above the body; then heat up the cautery so it has this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it turns white and drips blood. Then bring the testicles back to their place; and the minister should hold his hand over them so they don't return, and treat the groin area well, and put a pillow under him and a servant on each side of his legs, and another one on his feet holding his hands; then hold the cautery against the sign with your whole hand, keeping it straight and keeping it there until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, do it again until you hit the bone. Be careful that the testicles don't pop out when you're using the cautery so you don't burn him, and so that the patient doesn't die or suffer other ill effects.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you should know that when you don't reach the bone with the cautery, your work is for nothing. And the cautery for children should be smaller according to the size of their testicles, and for adults it should be larger according to their size; after 3 days, cure the area around the cautery with butter until the scalding is gone; then cure it with other ointments until it's healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well sewn up; and you should keep his testicles tied up for a long time so that they don't pop out when he stands up and walks around.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and against too much loud talking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will now describe the treatment by cutting in his chest.
de la routure dou ventre	of stomach ulcers
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they are not growing anymore, if he makes .a. cautery of the fire according to its quantity, and burns it to the third of his heart; after the cure according to what we have said. And some of the ancients have said that it must be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but first sign the incision and draw a line over the breadth above the ulcer, and another from below, and hold your hand steady throughout the cauterization. But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb, from falling or from injury, and the pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called a "point", and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness, and its condition of twisting and of its pain. If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, do another cautery upon it, for such is the custom, that it should change in the limb nearest to it, so that you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mixing of medicines is sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the disease that comes from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see this cauterized, take care if the disease is in its beginning, and is healed according to what we have said in the division, and does not stay or return, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then do 5 cauteries on the head: 1 on the crown of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and 2 on the 2 horns, and 1 behind on the nape; and let your hand be so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as much as the skin comes out so that the vapors of the gross humors may come out; and cauterize the wound according to what is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If the disease is scattered throughout the body, and it is clearly evident, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned: one cautery on the head, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large cautery on the groin, and one additional cautery on each hip; two cauteries on the elbows, two cauteries on the knees, one cautery on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the back of the heel. Sometimes a cautery is applied to the bone of the wrist, and one to the bone of the stomach, and one to the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And you should know that the more cauteries you apply, the more benefit they will bring to the patient; and you should know that the sick person does not feel pain from cautery as a healthy person does, because their body is already corrupted. The cauteries should be large or small depending on the limbs and joints, according to how you find them using the tools of iron. After cauterizing, treat the area with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but is not healed, then cauterize the limb according to its size; let the cautery be slightly penetrating into the depth of the vein. Then treat it with ointments until it is healed. Sometimes cautery is done on the hand, foot, or back, at the outlet of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; yet no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a moderately deep cautery according to the thickness of the vein, so that the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then treat it with a poultice of equal parts linseed and lentil flour, rose oil, and plantain leaves, as well as blood from the colon and almond blood. Mix everything together and apply it, binding it with a cloth and keeping it in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of sores by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer appears at the beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the edge of the cancer. And yet the wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen many times; and a more appropriate thing is that it is cauterized around, with the cautery called 'circle', as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called 'adubelati', and it is slow to die, either because of the superfluity that it causes or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, very old) and have little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries, pricking; after that, leave it as it is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all around with the cautery, then heat the cautery from which the form comes:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the skin, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it in a way that alleviates the course of the pustule. After the healing, once he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another type of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing more than a eaten-away member, for it eats away at the members just as fire burns dry branches. If you see this disease in a place that can withstand cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, some small and some large, according to what is needed in the location of the disease; then cauterize all over until you reach all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and place soft bandages soaked in oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed and all the corruption is gone. After the healing of the ulcers caused by fire, use ointments to generate flesh. And if you see after three days that new flesh has not yet grown, then restart the cautery on the parts that still have corruption. This eaten-away condition can sometimes be cured with medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the cure for medicine ague in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that in the feet due to coldness there arises a disease which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a large faulted growth that blisters the foot. And cauterization for this disease is according to two methods: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is such that you heat 1 cauterizing needle as much as an owl's feather, and it is made of good iron to the size that it can prop up the nail on all sides, and that it has thin edges; after, place it hot on the nail and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; and leave it thus for 3 days until it begins to secrete pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will drop off and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted to the body from coldness, and often happen in both hands and feet, then you must use hot water cautery; and it is in this way: take a brass or iron rod, or an owl's feather, and place it on the nail and the warts, that is to say, verrucous growths; and place the rod so that it presses all around, then pour a little hot water, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water a deep path to the root. Then let the patient endure the biting pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots. Thus do one after another, until you extract all those in the body, then cure them with ointments that promote healing.
li cure dou trembler	the shaking treatment
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other [ailments], you should make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spinous process; and one cautery on the penis, and one on the stomach with an olive-oil cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes they appear in the body as bathes or stinking pustules, which come from thick putrid matter. At their first appearance, one should make cauteries on each tip of the pustule: with a thin stick of myrtle, the tip taken into the fire, or with a long root of aristolochia, or with the lenticular cautery. Sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning as they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow any further, but the surplus from which they come is disrupted, and they are healed; but this should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are often great flowings of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery on the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, you must quickly put your index finger over the wound of the vein, and hold it very firmly until the blood is quiet under your finger and no drops issue forth; then take a number of olive-oil cauteries, both large and small according to the wound and the location where the artery runs, and apply the cautery to that vein where you are holding your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the bleeding starts again when you lift your finger from the wound and the cautery goes out, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is staunched; and be careful that you do not harm the nerve nearby, and that no other ill comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well staunched by itself if the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have described: by cautery, or by extraction if it is untreated, or by a strong ligature, or by medicines applied which have the power to staunch bleeding; and it should be bound and compressed skillfully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	He who administers a tight bandage or places hot objects on top, or similar things, will not benefit much if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and there is no medicine or healing available, then one should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and press firmly on the wound and the vein; and they should not move it but moisten it with cold water often so that it becomes very cold until the blood congeals and swells and becomes firm; and they should make a splint in front of what is needed for cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cauterization with fire or burning medicines, and their causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from the head to the foot, and I will continue in this chapter by the same way for what one can more easily find.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I may begin this, it is necessary, dear son, for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of that greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to be foolish. For people come in many ways to be healed. Some are so overcome by their illness that they would easily change it for the folly they find in their disease, and because of the greatness of their folly, one must fear for them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these there are some who give their consent and say: "Wait, I am cured." But the disease is stubborn. You must not consent to those who come to you with this attitude, but place more importance on your honor than on your desire, and do not act foolishly but wisely in what you are certain of, and from which you can take pride and profit; and use prophecy and indication in curing your illnesses so that salvation may be turned towards them. And this will help you achieve a good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have assigned this chapter to you in discussing the topic of cautery, according to what has been presented before in the chapter on cautery from head to foot, so that you can find more easily whatever you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You should know that this disease often comes to children during childbirth, and when the baby's head is squeezed too hard; and sometimes it comes from a relaxed cause that one does not know about.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease in adults; and of all those I have seen, death has always resulted; and for that reason, it seems best to me not to continue the treatment beyond a certain point.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and his head swelled every day until he could no longer bear it; and the moisture accumulated under the bone above the brain, between the heart and the bone. And if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, then you should make a large slit in the head, as long as two fingers, so that the moisture may flow out; and see the shape of the spatomile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the hollow is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of the head wider on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not close up again: then you must make three slits in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all moisture forcefully. After that, squeeze out the folds of clothes and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and cure the wound by tenting and poultices, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat with a little moisture as long as the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you observe where the aperture of the abscess is, and the gathering of the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the pus, and cut it according to what you can; and be careful not to cut the artery, and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the feet, and the disease is old, and the medicine does not help, then the last resort is cautery with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them open, the patient should bend his head back; then rub the area around the arteries with a rough cloth until they appear, then tighten the patient's neck all around with .i. cloth; then look where the vein bleeds, and the places are after the ears, and they are pressed down; then sign the spots in, then cut both with an acute spatulum of .ij. parts so that the incision reaches the bone, and this is through the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, cutting also .ij. fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the amount of space of three digits, then cut through and slit up to the bone; and what amount of blood is needed to be let out is 1/6 of a pint, and by chance a little more or less depending on what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains on the bone no trace of pus, so that hot abscesses do not come, then drain the wound and ligate it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	from the emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-age anemia comes, and catarrh is acute, due to moistors of the eyes and heat in the temples and ancient soddeness and similar things, and he has been treated by various methods of medicine and all of it does not help him, then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should let the hair of his temples grow, and feel for the artery in his temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not very swollen in some people who are too cold; and if it is swollen, then the patient should press on his neck with some folded cloth, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and anoint the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum made of this material:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then lightly scorch the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with tweezers, and carefully separate it from the tissue beneath in each part; and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the claw, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two joints. For if it is not cut off, the blood will not flow everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from 1/4 to 1/2 ounce, and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus will not come before the wound heals, and the blood will flow smoothly; then cut off the excess between the two ties in that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron knife up to the bone until the joints are cut; and this is the best way, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to end moisture; for this reason it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the hole with old cotton and puts it on top of well-made tenting; and when they are removed, they are cured with dry medicines that cause scabs to form, and with tenting, until it is healed; and if without cutting into the artery as much as you work at it, you hurry to cover it with cautery, or you use vitriol and press it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don't have this present, put a finger on the spot so that the blood is frozen, and moisten the spot with cold water so that the blood stops, and press it as it should be; and what is best and easier in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 2 parts, but the cutter must be very thick to retain its heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And between the two knives there should be a distance of one finger's width, and then when you have made an incision in both places, put the hot iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and keep the two heads apart because they are not welded together by this cautery; and this is how the cautery should be formed:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are falling from the eyes that are above the testicle of the head, and medicine does not help the healing, and you see the face of the sick person turning red, and there is movement in the front as if it were trembling; and when the oil is thin and moist so that the hair of the eyelids has fallen out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cure contused," and you shall do to the patient who has this disease that he lets the hairs grow on his forehead, then make .iiij cuts on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts be as .ij fingers all over the forehead going down to the nose, and the others .ij at .ij sides above the eyes, and beware of cutting the arteries that are on .ij sides above the eyes; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ij mandibles, and each wound be the quantity of .iij fingers across joint;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have ready a piece of sponge and a mouthful of cloth to wipe the blood, then pour the spathanium made of 2 parts of which this is the formula:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to be made on the temple up to the second incision; and scorch all the skin between the .ij cuts as far down as the cheek bone, then make another cut from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then take out this spathanium.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put into the first cut the instrument that is called "culter", and is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut the incision towards the breast bone and the soft part towards the bone, and tie it so that it comes to the middle slit. And press all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to the heart, and then make another cut in the middle slit up to the other side; and then draw out evenly and express the site for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton into each slit, and put wet clothes soaked in wine, oil, and garlic on top, and guard against hot abscesses coming; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer copious amounts of warm water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a sudden catarrh and you see the eyes are sunken and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and the hair falling out, and pain in the head, and the patient sneezing; then know from these symptoms that this matter and these catarrhs come from many veins, and the cure for it is to let blood.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you must instruct the patient to look up, then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another smaller one. Begin cutting from the left temple to the right, incising down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples' nerves that move the jaw. When the bone is exposed, use a sponge to soak up all the blood, then separate the two lips of the cut and insert old cotton, and tent with linen; then bind dampened cloths in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses. Once it is healed, you should rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat-flower and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; then administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	When the bone is exposed, use a sponge to soak up all the blood, then separate the two lips of the cut and insert old cotton, and tent with linen; then bind dampened cloths in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses. Once it is healed, you should rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote healing.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls from the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, minerals or similar objects like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans and lentils; or flowing substances like water, garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone or other object that does not adhere to the ear falls into it and does not grow in the ear, one should expose the ear to the sun. If you can see the stone, apply some violet oil or sisament oil and then remove it with forceps; have the patient sneeze while applying an ointment, plug the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and tie a piece of cloth or wool around the ear. Often the object will come out through this treatment; if not, it should be extracted with fine forceps, like these:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, use a thin, small pair of tweezers made of soft iron and insert their tips into the ear canal firmly; then stop the area around the tips with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the forceps; then pull it out firmly. Often it will come out in this way, as we have said. If not, take a glottis (a pair of forceps) similar to those used for birds and insert an instrument designed for this purpose, then put some cotton around it; press the glottis against the object, whether it is a stone or something else, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not come out with these methods, you should split the ear so that pus and blood come out, causing a chalazion  and spasm; the splitting method is as follows: first, bleed the patient's head, then make him sit between your hands and turn his ear upward, then make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat depends, and make the incision in the shape of a moon so that you can reach the stone; then extract it according to your ability, and suck it firmly with your mouth until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatumile tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And administer incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to moisture in the ear until you have made many pieces; then extract it with small pincers and a suction cup, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the eardrum where the pain is, the patient should use snuff of the first remedies, and fill the ear with old cotton. And he should lie on that same ear where the pain is. If the pain jumps out through the ear, that's good. If not, take many thin and light stones according to the length of your finger, and heat them in fire; and insert one end of his finger into the ear, and press down with the other part, and place another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to do this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out; and if you see that, take a straw, and put one end into the ear, and the other end heat with fire until the thin straw is burnt; then do the same with another straw until all the water comes out, as we have said in the case of the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the insect, if it is of a small body, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of a large body that can be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section on distillations, and if the treatment is not effective, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take a sample of the fluid where the pain is located.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is narrow below and wide above. And insert the thinnest end of a rod into the ear according to the amount of pain from the malady; then suck forcefully at the entire rod, doing this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
