If they do not come out, stop up the ear with cotton as I said for the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for the extraction of worms, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, from which the pain is originating, just as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it can be made of silver or brass with small holes below and a wider opening above for distillation; and to press the distillation into the instrument use a well-made brass rod, and if you see fit, wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you use, into the rod, and let the rod be in the ear; then put the rasor, filled with cotton, into the ear, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and he feels the medicine inside, and let the distillation be a little warm, as one would heat it over fire to distil it into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the cleaning of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an earhole; and the same thing happens to adults due to the cleaning of a wound or a cyst inside the ear. This cleaning sometimes opens a perforation in the eardrum, which cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a small defect, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when there is an opening that cannot be seen, it is a sign of a poor prognosis in many cases. In such cases, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun and examine it. If you can see the perforation clearly, then its appearance indicates the nature of the disease:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be narrow and sharp in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear. If the perforation is due to a cyst or body part in the ear, then one should hold it with fine tweezers and gently scrape away at it until all the foreign matter is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the wax is impacted in the ear, take a small, thin rasp and heat it slightly in the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear. If you feel the wax which the patient feels aching when he hears, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the aperture, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, then take a tent and moisten it in rosewater, and powder over vitrialed vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is appropriate to draw out the tent and move another tent moistened with cerotum made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then clean it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, take a sponge and dip it in cold water, and apply it to the ear, and use other remedies which stop the bleeding that come from distilling treatments.
de la char des papieres	from the ash of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This treatment involves papers on the eyes when they are moist and dry; you should then extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the head of a spatula from its roots; then place powdered vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is without skin, one should cauterize it with a thin lens, and the cautery after the incision will help; and many times they return, as long as something remains in their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come as papers of things that look like hail in their shape and hardness, and this is why the disease is called "hailstorm"; it is a gathering of moisture, large in the paper above and below; its work is such: first, if the hailstone moves from side to side, and it is light enough to know, then they open it with tweezers and pinchers, and pull off the head. If the split is large, there should be a stitch, and the wound treated until it heals; but if it is small, no force should be used, for the ointment will restore and heal it quickly.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then reverse the paper, and hold the hailstone with pincers, and press from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, wash the eye with salted water, and clean the place of that which causes pain until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinah is a fat that is woven into the paper above, and this happens most to children with no adults, and it affects their eyes greatly, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot look at sunlight because the tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this, they lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids become moist which covers the swelling and appearance of the exinah which opens in the eye. And when you press on the area with your fingers and feel the exinah between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of treatment is that the patient puts his head on yours; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinah from each part, and then place it over him; and press with your fingers from both sides, so that the exinah is gathered within the circle. Then cut through the moisture with the spatulum, making a slit no larger than the wound made in the vein when opening it; and in some cases, the exinah comes out of the slit according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	So take a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and turn your hand to the left and right until it is stretched; and be careful not to push into the fissure so that you do not go all the way to the sphenoid bone up to the eye, lest you damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then widen the fissure slightly so that it opens; then withdraw as we have said, then moisten a piece of cloth in vinegar and water, and apply it to the spot, and draw out with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind their teeth and put something on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then he should be cured until he is healed. And if there is a hot abscess at the site, then he should be cured with soothing poultices until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hair from papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers and are not of their nature, and they harm the eyes, causing various diseases such as tears, softness of the papers, and albuginea, leading to destruction of the eyes; the cure is according to four methods: through cauterization with fire, or with medicine water according to what comes before the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or with splints, according to what I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then hold the paper of the eye in your left hand; if it turns easily, that is good; if not, insert a needle with thread through the paper, either at the edge or where the hair is growing, and pass the thread over the entire paper, then hold it against the razor; next, cut into the skin under the paper, under the aberrant hairs, up to the great tear duct and down to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the paper; mark a figure on the paper, like a holly leaf, but adjust the shape according to the amount you see the divided paper rising.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a large amount of divided paper due to moisture, one must cut out the paper according to the amount it has softened; then cut into the skin along the two lines you marked, starting from the great tear duct and ending at the small one; make one incision near the natural hair in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle in one of the angles of the wound, and lift the skin entirely; then bring together the two lips with a single stitch using a fine woolen thread and an aiguille, and wipe away the blood; and dry up any surplus thread above the two eyelids with any sticky substance you like, if you wish to do so; otherwise, leave the stitch and threads in place for three or four days; then remove the stitch and treat the wound with dry, constrictive substances, for the paper will adhere on its own once the wound heals, but the stitch is painful (as the ancients say), and this method is without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and in another way: and it is that you draw the paper with a shape that is like the myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three notches according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is on top into small pieces evenly according to the shape that is there:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the tweezers and it is not even, take a needle with which there is .i. thread, and push it into the figure; and another thread from near the large artery, and the second thread from near the small one, and pull the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have described, then bring the two lips of the wound together with a stitch, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with cerate and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the paper's hairs are reversed: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of bones is as follows: turn the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, then make two bones by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatulum; then tie two knots at each end where you hold the threads; then assemble them skillfully above what is on top of the paper of the eye, and pull out the two bones from their formed parts; and leave it for a few days, and the skin that was pulled will die, become numb, and fall off, as it heals.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is slow to heal, if the cut still hurts, then treat it until it heals; and when the wound is sewn up and the paper lifted, the hairs will no longer hurt; and this is the form of the two bones you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the procedures are such that you pierce a thin needle and thread in it with a fine silk thread; then assemble the eyes and tie them skillfully, and let the length of the threads be about a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the case and tie it at its end; then put the patient's head on your hand; and have it exposed to the sun so that the procedures are revealed, for this is a subtle and delicate procedure, then pierce the needle all the way through the paper until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the case, and thread that hair into the case, whether there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs are drawn outward through the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the pustule is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you shall treat the pustule from underneath to the very end that you have directed, until the pustule comes out from above the opening, and you see it with your eye; then you shall draw out the pustule and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place, and new skin forms over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from the eyebrows, and let them grow together until they are stretched out, and then cut them.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye pustule
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "alacrati" or "eye pustule" occurs, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly due to injury, surgery, cauterization, or similar causes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat it is to split the wound and separate its edges, then put in a tent of linen and apply a poultice until it is healed; and one must not use in its treatment anything that would dry it out or constrict it. For if you do, the disease will return worse than before; but rather use softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or watered-down wine with ground linseed, and apply an ointment of softened diaquilon in one of the oils, and cover it with a tent, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must be careful that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, but only to prevent it from returning to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	from the pus that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is under the eye and is truly called "axacrati", has natural and accidental causes. The accident comes from wounds, incisions, cauterization, and similar things; and the way to treat it is to take a needle with a double thread, and pierce it through the flesh so that the thread goes into the left tear duct and emerges on the right, and then the flesh above the needle is cut away, leaving a 1.5 cm wide flap.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns to what it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper over, and make 2 incisions along the edges of the paper; and let the edges of the 2 incisions be at the 2 angles of the incision that you have cut, and make angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter "J" in Greek; then remove this flesh, according to the amount that its sides are cut under, from what follows the paper, then join the 2 separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it with the medicines we have mentioned for softening, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crack or a wound or cautery, then one should make a plain slit under the hair of the skin, and according to what is above; then draw between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares machines with all his power how he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of operations and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden movement of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness happens to the skin in such a way that the paper above is separated from the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then one should push the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it upwards; and they are held by tweezers, so that you grab what is open on the surface of the staphitis, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot bear for the staphitis to be too sharp or to cut into the eye; and your incision, by which you scrape this union, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all of this union is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is a salty water, and it is lifted with sweet water, and a collarette; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put over the eye soft lamb's wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day use the collar and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail has two forms: it is nervous and resembles a hard cyst; the other is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture which, when touched with iron and crushed between pincers, cannot be crushed by anyone; and both types originate from the lower eyelid, growing little by little until they cover the entire eye, its light, and its movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the incision is that the patient places his head on your lap, then opens his eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then grab the nail with pincers made of thin metal, and pierce it at the top; then take a needle, thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or ox's hair, through it, and double its point over and insert it into the nail, and tie the nail to the thread, and extend it upwards, then scrape away all around the nail where the eyelid continues towards the tear duct until you reach the soft tissue; then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with gentle motions, using a delicate instrument, and leave the natural skin of the eyelid, so that no incision comes into contact with the tear duct, as we have said; then extend the nail to the little finger only, and tie it to the thread, as we have described.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the instrument does not touch and break the carnous membrane, and that the tear duct is not pierced; and after the incision, apply a little ground chalk to the eye, and a collar made of linen soaked in it, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, nor can the hooks enter, many times this kind of nail is cured by medicine; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, then work on the eye of the disease, and take the spatulum slightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently lift up the nail and if you see that it does not diminish and the inflammation draws near, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red copper ore and powdered, and stop up the eye until the next day; then begin again the other work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin again the work as before, until it is healed.Et se il y aveit aposteme froid, adonques cure l’aposteme par le chaus; et si tu vois qu’elle ne voulent point arder, si distille en l’oil du vin de groseille, et du coliere dou ver, et du litargire, et du sal amoniac; et si la chose n’est pas trop chaude, si peit de ta bouche.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eyelid hurts in the eye with great harm, then suspend it on the hook and scrape off a part but not all so that no body of tears comes into it; then distill into the eye red copper ore made from litharge.And if the appearance of the flesh around the eyelid hurts in the eye with great harm, then suspend it on the hook and scrape off a part but not all so that no body of tears comes into it; then distill into the eye red copper ore made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	In some men there sometimes grows red flesh over the pupil, covering it and pushing it back against the eyeball, resembling a rose-colored bulbous flower. The treatment for this is for the patient to press his head against something solid, then open his eyes wide, and then cut off all of that flesh with nails or a similar tool, holding tightly with one hand; next, cut away the first piece of flesh, and keep cutting all the way to the root, being careful not to scratch the eyeball during the procedure. The incision should be made with a sharp instrument, as we have described in the section on incisions for fingernails, and with gentle pressure so that the instrument can penetrate the flesh;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	once the incision is complete and all of the flesh has been removed, apply eye salve made from egg yolk and red wine vinegar, and cover the eyeball with cotton padded with egg white so that it is protected from hot abscesses; if nothing remains, and the white part of the eye turns red, then leave it alone and treat the abscess with remedies for hot abscesses; then return to the treatment until the eye is healed, and do this for as many times as necessary.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary to adapt the treatment based on whether the condition is natural or accidental, and to use tools made of iron; do not insert your fingers in any of these treatments until you see that the patient can tolerate it.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that cover the eye, and they obscure vision and weaken the eye every day. Therefore, first you should examine the eye to see if it is healthy and normal, and not suffering from any other condition beyond the red veins; then proceed thus: instruct the patient to tilt his head back so that you can reach the eyelids, and with a delicate instrument, according to your skill, grasp and lift the lower eyelid gently, making sure to use a double-edged tool according to this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And two edges in .I. body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then draw gently on the veins with a subtle force, and let the blood out an hour after another, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to wound the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not touch anything beyond the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the sebaceous material.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot pull out all of this in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with soothing things for the pain of them, and let it be for several days until the pain is assuaged and the hot abscess is secured, then begin again according to this method which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon should examine the "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a hole in it that you must open over the abscess, where it should remain, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you will see the corruption and blackness, then return to all of the instrument by which this form is made; and it is called a "sharp point", and it should be made to pierce one tip, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the fistula is closed and new skin has formed, and the body of the bow is closed, and remains in this way for 40 days, and does not renew itself and there is no bad accident, you know that it is healed; if not, then there is nothing else to do but to open the fistula at the opening of the nose according to this form: then you remove the bone a second time with an iron instrument, and with watery medications, and when it has been removed, take .a. forest according to this form, and let the head of the iron be .ai. angles, and let the staff be thinned at the top as far as you can see in the picture:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then put it on the bone next to the earring, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn all the way through the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through his nose; then restore the site with dry medications as I have taught you, and when the skin forms and hardens, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye:
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully, and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you should ligature the patient; then let it heal, then put leeches or suckers without piercing, then apply a poultice of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, then bandage it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the bandages is that you take soft bandages, doubling each one four times, then place them one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then tighten it from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the leeches without piercing to suck; then remove the leeches and leave the eye tight day and night, and if the ligature softens, you must tighten it much; then remove the ligature after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice, bandages, ligature, and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in a woven cloth, then it opens and comes out like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread of the upper arm; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then pull on the place of the double thread and tie one part of the weave tightly, then pull out the needle and put a wet lamb's wool over the eye; and let it be until the threads cut through the weave, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the weave on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give a strong indication, he should pierce them with a sharp spatulum which comes from under the eye, and dry up the white moistness and draw down the eyes, and then let him enter immediately; then he should extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but an inflammation of the eye socket, resembling water but not being water; and the way that it appears to be treated is for the patient to sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take hold of his head with both hands and move it until you see the socket coming towards your eyes; then it should remain there, and the light should not disappear and the patient should see things as he used to. And if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the swelling of the socket does not appear as we have said, take hold of the patient's head with both hands and take the sharp spatulum and put it on the white of the eye gently and move it until the socket comes out; then drop warm honeyed water into the eye, or water or fenugreek which has been boiled and mixed with honey, and then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of the ulcers in the division, and what is needed to pierce it; then work according to health. You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light so that the sun does not affect him, and close and hold his healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper over the eye if the ulcers are on the left side, or on the right side if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the ulcers are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that part of the eye where the tear duct is located, then carefully insert the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand so that it pierces the white of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches the hollow; the depth of the path of the almagda should be equal to the thickness of the space between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horn-like membrane, and then insert the instrument as far as the place where the ulcer is, then express it under one path after another. If the ulcer drains now, the patient sees in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the ulcer rises again through the second path, press it with the instrument; and when it is firmly lodged and does not rise, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand slightly back and forth; then put in the ulcer a little seal gem, and remove it from that eye. Then moisten a cotton ball or lamb's wool in rose oil and bind it over the eye with the healthy eye. We, and those of our time, place on it crushed comfrey with plenty of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deeply but make a slender slit, then insert alum, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient a dark chamber in which he can sleep on his back in a dim place; and let him be deprived of all movement, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and let him be bound according to his condition for three days; then release him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then re-bind him until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the operation or after the incision now, but you should alleviate it, so that the fluid may ascend gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And if a hot abscess comes, release the eye before the seventh day, and use that which soothes abscesses; and when it is soothed, release the vision and place upon his face an eyelid to cover one eye, and let him be in that dark room again. And then exit the room little by little, and return to his condition; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Land of Israel who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and they suck out the fluid, but nonetheless I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books by the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.

de la char sor le neis	of the eye socket towards the nose.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes there are various types of nosebleeds that emerge from the nose, some resembling scorpions with feet-like tips; and among them, there are those with a dark-colored swelling and others with a light-colored one. For the latter type, which is not swollen, you should make the patient lean back towards the sun, pinch his nose shut, and pour the blood into those veins, pulling them outward; then press hard on what you can sustain using a very sharp and subtle pair of tweezers from one side until you are sure that the vein has been completely blocked.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing which cannot be covered, open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without it swells or an abscess forms, dry it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the corruption is removed, then pour on wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose works and moisture comes to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is corruption in the bone above, and the instruments do not work to cut it: therefore you must place a thread of linen about a finger thick into his nose at his own will, and let it hang down from one nostril between each nostril by a distance of a finger or less; and let the patient hold the end of the thread in his mouth with his hand as far as he can, and draw it through to the palate; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes from the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and pull them gently towards each other so that you know that they have touched the corruption, then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all the corruption; and then place a plug of cotton in the nostril for several days until it is healed, and if he needs dry medicines, use them. This is the instrument used to cleanse the nose, through which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit should also be made of the same material; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the nose; and it should have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the diaphragm
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the diaphragm, and grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to the eye; therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all of it, then place the cautery or burning medicine on top; and if one delays cutting until it has become large, then beware if it is hard, of dark color, and lacking in feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is an ulcerated abscess, because when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due only to pressure, not due to dark color, and you see that one can cut it all away, then evacuate the patient and cut it without fear, and clean the area of dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the heart is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should know that when pus of a continuous flow comes from one of these damaged cartilage areas, it does not benefit some people as much as others. Therefore, whenever this happens to someone, you should examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then attach the .ij. lips with a stitch, then clean it until it heals; and if the lips are separated on both sides, you should scrape all parts of their heart until they heal, then stitch the .ij. lips together, tighten them, and powder them with dragon's blood and incense; place a piece of strong plaster or other healing plaster over the powders, and leave it to heal by itself, then clean it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore, you should turn the lips inside out, and slit them on each knob, and pinch and cut into each part; then apply crushed vitriol to the incision, until the blood is stanched; then use the leechwort, and cleanse the area of dry matter until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow out; then place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, and this often happens, then these are the forms of estrume for coping.
des sordens	of the eyes, and to the
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Some are clustered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and some are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, so that the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so you should have the patient sit in your lap, and open his mouth wide, and inspect the teeth where the sores appear, until nothing remains; and thus you should do for blackness, and yellowness, and other discoloration, until they are clean; and if one is removed at first, it is good; if not, then repeat it again the next day or the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of estrume to remove them, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the rasors with which one scrapes the teeth have different forms from those with which one scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure a tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because no one should do this; because it is a very high substance until there is no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is forced to pull out the tooth, you should be sure of the toothache. Many times the pain deceives the patient and believes that it is in a healthy tooth and makes them pull out a good tooth; and yet the pain does not go away through this, until the evil root is removed, because we have already tried this with these doctors; and when you are quite sure of the toothache, you should scrape around the tooth all around. Open your mouth wide to push back the gum from all sides; then grab the tooth with your fingers or with thin tweezers at the very tip, and pull it out little by little until it is well loosened, then hold the tweezers tightly; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling out the tooth straight without breaking it, if it does not jump out, take one of these instruments and put it inside on each side, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and rotted, you should fill it with cloth where the holes are; and hold it tightly with tweezers so that it does not break while being pulled; and it is necessary to work gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And then he must move all around his gum and gum, as he did before, until the tooth comes out, as it is said, without moving it. And after that, he should wipe his gum from pulling gently; and let his head be in your lap between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move, and move the gum where the tooth came out, as he did before.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, which make the teeth loose, have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be made of large pieces so that they don't bend during pulling, and be made of good iron, and be serrated to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during pulling, you should put wet cotton on the area for one or two days, until the gums are softened. Then use forceps, which are called "algefri", to grip the tooth like a pair of pliers; they should be made with teeth like a file, and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and insert the instrument called 'althali', that is, forceps, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Let it be sturdy and strong so as not to break, and if the root pops out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And let one assist with this instrument which has .ij. tips, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master subtlety finds by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it does not break in the cart or the other bones, or it protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, so here is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is a protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then cut it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then cut it, and if there is an air-bubble with the tooth, take this instrument, of which here is the shape, and it is like a small beak, and it should be made of iron with a sharp point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum recedes little by little day by day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that one can be filed down, then file it with a file such as this, according to its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little day by day gently, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with a rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose:
