Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front teeth loosen, whether from a blow or from falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rot, but gold never moves; and the wire should be medium-thin or thick, depending on the amount of space between the teeth. And if you want to direct the teeth, take the wire and wind it double between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, so that you reach the loose tooth on the other side; then pull your hand gently and tightly, so that it does not move. Then grab the wire with a pair of tweezers and assemble it, and tie them together between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, so that it does not cut the tongue; and leave it as tightly as possible for as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone or the wire breaks, then tie it with another wire. It will remain this way for as long as you want, and this is the shape of the teeth and the form of guiding the two healthy teeth, whether there are one or more loose teeth, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is reset in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and it is placed in the gap where the defect is, and it is held there as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound in the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this condition occurs naturally, and sometimes it is caused by an injury; and the treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, and press his tongue against your hand, and then lift the tongue up; next, cut the nervous membrane under the tongue, so that the tongue is separated from its attachment, and if there is any swelling or wound, and this is due to a recent injury, then insert a needle and cut the membrane under it; and be careful not to cut too deeply, so as not to injure the artery below. And when you have finished, rinse the area with rose water or cold water, and then place a linen tent under the tongue; and every night apply a plaster to the affected area, so that the skin cannot heal. And if there is any bleeding, apply crushed vitriol; and if the bleeding continues, cauterize it with a lentiginout cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat the wound with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it has turned purple or black, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to become a blister, and there is moisture, then insert the needle, and open it with a thin spatumile, and release it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your treatment, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you draw out everything. Then rinse the area with rose water and salt water, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are sometimes swellings in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called tonsils. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if they are hard abscesses of a small size and a dusky color, do not touch them with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron because of the blood flow; but let it be until it bursts, or it will burst on its own. And if it is white in appearance and the root is thin, have an instrument ready to lance, but first check that the abscess is calm and soothed. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and he should open his mouth and the assistant should hold his hands between his jaws and press his tongue down under the instrument, with which the lancing will be done; it should be made of silver or thin bronze like a dagger.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue against this instrument, and see the abscess, take a needle and insert it into the tonsil, and pull it out above as hard as you can; and draw out some of the pus with it, then cover the instrument again, so that it is ready for use. It has a very sharp point, and the tip curves in one direction or another, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cover it with tongs, of which the shape is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is cut on one side, and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or with scorched pomegranate peels, or with bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two glands appear in the throat, so cut them then just as the two glands are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely, one abscess of small size; and it had almost closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like this for one or two days. And the abscess had become so large that it had pushed out two bumps from the openings of the nose. I quickly took action, and inserted a needle into one opening, then drew out a lot of pus; then I did the same at the other nasal opening, and cleared her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards, I inserted the needle into the abscesses, and cut out a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passageway in the throat of the woman was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied, so it became very large; therefore, I packed it and cauterized it inside her throat; thus it did not grow anymore; and I left these parts, and she was in the hands of God after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When a catarrh descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an "eye". When it has been cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the surrounding abscesses are soothed, and it is delicate, then you should cover it; and if it is round and not long, and blood-red, or yellow, or black, then you should avoid cutting into it, for there is great danger to the patient. Therefore, when you see it according to the way I have described, in terms of its whiteness and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument that we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it down, and cover it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for cutting into the two almonds. You must not cut deeper than the natural limit; otherwise, you will harm the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said about the cure in the incision of the two almonds, until it is healed. If the patient fears having it covered, then you should use a cautery to treat the fear. The method of cauterization is as follows: the patient puts his head down, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we mentioned earlier; he breathes in very hot air, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and uses this implement, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and the instrument is pressed into the eye with all the medicine; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from the mouth due to the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat and cause vomiting; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it become numb and the stinging of the medicine is soothed. If you see something, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton on the eyelid, so that the cotton lies on the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for four or five days. If you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery wash around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take calendula and hyssop and marjoram and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and mix them all or some of them into one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. The pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and the pot has a handle shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it can be made of silver or bronze, and one of the tools is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise to the eye through the tube, until the eye is deadened; then repeat often until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, because many things can happen; nor should you do this except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put an egg white inside it, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg white does not allow the vapors to burden the mouth, and this is a good and safe treatment.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, becomes lodged in the throat; therefore you should try to remove whatever you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the entire instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not reveal itself and is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a string to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches its destination, it will stick there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of soft lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and the tip should be lifted upward; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or it may be torn, nor should you push the bone in; and move it so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can feel where the object is stuck; then he should swallow the instrument, or pull it out with the instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the blood is stopped by medicine, as I have said in the division, through the use of remedies; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you about. And if you see any blood, draw it out with a very small hook, or with fine tweezers suitable for this purpose. And if this does not work, take a small knife, insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the tip of the knife and do this frequently. And if the disease is caused by water, take a full glass of cold water, open his mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, moving his hand frequently; and as soon as the blood comes into contact with the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not stop as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I described for smoking out the throat; do this many times, for it will surely work. And the way to smoke him is to place burning charcoal in a pot with a perforated lid, and insert the tip of the instrument into the hole; then blow your smoke into the pot, and let the patient hold the knife in his mouth, closing his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the blood; and the blood will stop immediately. If it does not, repeat the smoking many times. And let the patient be thirsty, eating salted and dry things, and drinking no water; and then he will surely pass the blood through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to draw out the blood is, when one can see it, like curved tweezers that can enter the throat; it is similar to a surgeon's forceps, and has roughness from lime, so that it can grasp firmly. See its shape here:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many types of abscesses, depending on their appearance, as the recollections that follow this in this book show, and they differ in puncturing and size; and there are two main types, one is the same in its appearance, and the other is due to the location in the body. Abscesses in the head are different from those in the foundations, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that occur in joints, and each type has a different treatment method.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And with some abscesses one must not puncture them until the pus is mature according to its completion; and there are others that one must puncture when they become ripe, without waiting for their completion, such as those near joints. For if an abscess comes near a joint, and you leave it until it becomes pus-filled around the joint, it can corrupt the ligament and nerve of the joint, causing contraction in that member. If the abscess is by a principal member, and you delay puncturing it until it is mature, it will harm the principal member. But if it is near the foundation, one must puncture it so that it may mature; and one must not puncture an abscess before its completion has been digested, except for those by the foundation, which may become pus-filled and elongated inside without causing a fistula, and may heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the rupture of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the rupture in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the rupture be made in the longest part of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and on nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that fold, according to the part of the body. And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the rupture remain until digestion is completed and as we have said. For if you pierce it before that, it lengthens the body with venom from it, and it is full of filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it harden. And for some abscesses which are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.  And you must treat small abscesses with small openings; and large abscesses with large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and in some there is a chewed kernel, and it is covered when it has become as soft as a grape, and is dead, as one does with blisters: and in some they are split into three angles, and some are covered like the leaf of a myrtle, as in abscesses of the fingers; and in some an circular incision is made, and other incisions and similar covers.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those which have no head, as in a superficial abscess, you must pierce it directly; and when the abscess is large, and it has drawn much pus, and you cannot draw out all of it at once, then stop the abscess, then the next day draw out some more; do this repeatedly until all the pus is discharged; likewise if the patient is of feeble constitution, or a woman carrying a child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man. For sometimes the pus jumps out with the release of the pus sac and the patient may not notice it; therefore be very careful in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, wash the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, dress it with tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then plug each opening with a tent so that they come against one another; and if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and chewed it all around, then fill it with old cotton or the lint from a linen cloth without moisture, and let it lie for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times. And if the bleeding persists, apply a poultice and treatment, and the powders I have described earlier in this book; and if it is wintertime, and the abscess is very nervous, then you should place warm tents and cloths moistened with wine and hot oil over it; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place moist cloths over it, wetted with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil for a third of the day, as we have said; then open the abscess, wash it out, and treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you should know generally about the treatment of abscesses; I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter on it.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are like us, like the jaw of a chicken, and there is much resemblance to it. There is fat and suchlike in them, where there is moisture as well as pulp; and there are those which are hard and stony-like in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not do the opposite. The action of the body is that you must test with all .i. instrument called 'entromissoire', from which form comes afterwards, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then they make it from above, long. And when the moisture is evacuated, it scabs without leaving anything behind, the skin that contains that moisture; for it returns again when one leaves nothing behind; then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who stay overnight should do the same. And then start the cotton again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it stays no longer overnight; then cure the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains .i. piece of fat, cut it according to this form, from above; and let out your fingernails, and scrape it all over, and put all your care into drawing it out under the skin where it lies; and if the artery does the opposite, do what I told you after. And so do with the abscess if it is stony, and in terms of cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on the stony abscess and moisture is lighter, because they contain little blood. And there are some of these abscesses in the head where there is no moisture, and one of these was an abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had made an incision, it would have done just as much harm as a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, other than those that come to the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be in the most dependent part, so that mucous can exit; and cure them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	There are many types of scrofula, some containing moisture and others that do not respond to treatment. When you find one that is soft to the touch, has a similar color to the rest of the body, and does not pulsate or press on any nerves, vessels, or ducts, and is not deep, then you should cut it open and scrape away at each part. The two lips of the heart should be pinched together if necessary, as mentioned earlier regarding abscesses in the head; draw it out little by little, being careful not to cut any nerves or veins, and without using a spatula or knife so that the hand does not slip. Do not cut too deeply, only as much as you need to.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If you cut into a vein or artery and it will not allow you to work, put vitriol powder or any other blood-stopping powder in the wound and press on it; then leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound softens and begins to suppurate. When the blood has clotted, return to your task and finish it; then check if there are any small scrofula remaining, cut and clean them. If there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, do not cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread and let it drop off without causing harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When cutting out the entire scrofula, you should bring together and sew closed the two lips of the wound so that no superfluity remains due to the size of the scrofula. Then you should attend to cutting away at its root and drawing it out as mentioned before. For scrofula that contain superfluity, pierce where it seems to be dying; then pierce it in the same way as mentioned earlier, allowing for an outlet, and then treat it with poultices containing ointment and similar remedies so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption. Once the wound is clean, dress it with ointment and a poultice of charred wood until it heals.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is a written record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, the flap of skin in the throat known as the "epiglottis" should be cut; and this is done to aid them, because all the veins and the pormon are affected by the illness in those who have a hot abscess in their mouth, or in their throat or in both testicles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pormon, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid loss of life due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it underneath three circles or four, a small split across, between two circles or according to the amount of the split in the hyoid, not at all in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places if they are suitable for the splitting of the epiglottis so that there is no bone, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the masters are fearful, they must extend the skin of the throat to the entire length, then split the meat until it reaches the larynx; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the hyoid, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the splitting of the windpipe of the larynx which jumped out through the opening that was broken, and by the defect of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed that we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines which promote flesh growth, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the deficiency of blood has been restored.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, one should press on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and for this reason the ancients commanded that the wound remain open until the mischief of the disease was passed, and it is passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take a knife and stick it in her throat, cutting some of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood had come out of it, and that she had not coughed up any phlegm or spittle except what came out through her throat, and the wind was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was cured;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the lady had nothing but hoarseness, and returned afterwards to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	so that in the cutting of the epiglottis, one need not fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess the color of saffron, and it occurs often in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; a natural hernia has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents happen in two ways, one of which resembles a cyst, and the other way is like an abscess that comes out of an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear in them, and one should not operate on them using force unless they are small, and test and examine all the openings:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a cyst, and it cannot move at all, then cut it as one would cut a cyst, and pull it out with tweezers if there is any hair;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and look inside thoroughly, and treat it as it should be treated until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of us, of which I will tell all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must say about the difference between us and an issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is a fever and chills while the eruption has not yet passed and the rash is complete; then the fever and chills cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With no heat or fever, and no pain, and it contains a syphilis, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to their appearances, either dry or moist, and much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of the nose, test and examine it first with all the instruments called "endoscopic", according to what its shape will allow in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of examining abscesses in the nose is that you press the moistest part that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the forceps, and take care of what jumps out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If pus flows freely, whatever its color, treat it as I have described for other abscesses:
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if no pus flows after the forceps are used, know that it is sluggish, so they must make a cross-cut and take it with tweezers and gently scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it stays in place, it will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays for a while, and the pain bothers you, then employ some corrosive powders on the wound, and hold the wound, and apply hot poultices to soothe the abscess, and treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the abscess is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which causes pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is bleeding profusely, and it is contrary to you or another, then quickly apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two days or three until the wound festered and stop the bleeding; then return to covering what has been left exposed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments for probing, and they come in three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of probes called 'albaret', and one type called 'breb'; and there are three types of these, large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses and fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are similar to the needles used for sorcery, made of brass, iron, or silver; and the yellow-tinted ones are better, and more tested with black pitch, for probing the curvatures of fistulas.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They come in three types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the knives are of many similarities, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are knives with .1 curve in three ways as well.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if there are onions with .iij curves, and they are also in .iij ways; and if there are onions with .ij curves, and onions with only one curve, and they are in .iij ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these which are used for cutting are sharp, and there are some which do not cut except from one side, so that we do not cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and among these introducers are those with handles placed on them so that the patient does not hurt themselves when opening abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are in .iij ways: large, small, and medium, as you can see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use it on bare flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes another small instrument is made, like slices of a fist, according to this form, with which blood is stopped:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the area that heals by stopping the flow of blood from the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are cut according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they become infected, so that they look like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and those who want to cure them must bleed according to this form from b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then burn the fat, and fill the wound with ointment, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and heal it until it is cured;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags down and becomes saggy due to its size as it does in women, then make two cuts above, at two similar places;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one cut is next to the other at the end of each line, and so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this form, from b. to g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then burns the skin between the two lips and removes the fat, and applies what we have said about sutures and powders, and what is necessary for healing, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient will not rest, or due to blood flow, you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it absorbs the remaining pus and fat, then heal it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpit
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	This abscess that comes under the armpit is like a hard scrofula, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess has been drained, employ the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, they should proceed as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound becomes pus-filled, they should apply cauterization as we have described earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, this often leads to abscesses forming, and similarly with a vein that is swollen and abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows it is due to an artery, the abscess will be long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a pulling; and when it is due to a vein, there is a cold, numb feeling.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpit and in the groin and neck and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	One should therefore avoid the cure of iron, and one who is at the head should also avoid it, as well as one who has inflammation of an artery that bursts through the skin of the neck;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then open the incision with a scalpel, and carefully cut the artery away from the veins, so that it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle under the artery, and pierce it all the way through to the other side, and compress the artery with a double thread in .2 inches, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point to the location between the two ties of an intruder so that the pus flows out and the abscess is drained.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment that turns yellow, until the wound heals over.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with an appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to a wound in that location, then you should dye your hand with the pus from the abscess all over the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the area you are holding in your hand, and pierce it, and put .i. double thread on it, so that you can pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, on one of its two sides with the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you are afraid the thread will come undone, then tie another needle to all .i. thread underneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in .iiij. ways;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then scrape the abscess so that the excess comes out, then scrape the excess from the skin and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they come to the nerves when they are hurt, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is a type of abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it has various dispositions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is firmly held, the patient feels pain, and it is not in a superficial part of the body, but deep under the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and must be completely still, and not move forward or backward, nor down or up, and those who have dislocations should not have their joints covered by iron; otherwise, they might contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And those who are on the head or forehead, use the skullcap.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, he should suspend it from the hook, and scrape it, then cut out the bone and stitch up the wound to heal it.
des grosses boces pendans	large bumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes they occur in bellies and nowhere else; this is a disease called "fungus" because of their resemblance to nuts, and it has a thin root and the bumps are large; there are small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two on his belly which looked more like fungi than anything else; there was no other difference, they were white and had thin roots, and they oozed moisture when cut.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I examined them and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6. The treatment for the incision is to look at whether the patient's joint is moist, and the color of the articulation is white and moist with a delicate root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the cut is too large for the spatula, and the blood flows profusely, then hasten to cauterize it. For in cutting there are often great flow of blood, and if it does not stop, then quickly apply the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see that the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision with the iron, take a well-prepared thread and tie it around the articulation as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then release it, and keep tightening the thread until he copes the articulation, and if the roots are large, he may fear to cope the entire articulation at once due to the pain; but you can cope half of it first,and then come back later to cope the other half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound and be careful not to cover the thistle which is of a foul colour and poor odour and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a deep abscess, and I will come to the treatment of sores next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a wound or a fissure in a ulcer, and it is on the belly and some of the bowels, as it happens in other ulcers, or from blood coming from veins or arteries, according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is through the rupture of the sinus and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles that of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and discharges from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it recoils, and then returns, and sometimes it becomes serrated, and grows larger at the entrance of the bath and from great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a minor issue, and it opens easily when you press it with your hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, then it opens through these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to the rupture of the bowel and the sinus, then the color resembles that of the body, and it discharges from various outlets, and it is a light thing without pain; and if it is due to wind, then there is swelling in the touch, and the procedure is to examine whether the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If you must let it heal. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is in the intestines or bowels, then you must instruct the patient to tighten his belt and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the stomach.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	Then command him to lie still between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the area that you have signed all over the stomach,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut half of the abscess from the top down to the large claw;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it tightly with a strong thread or strong silk cord, and let the patient keep it clean;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then cut half of the abscess that extends above the string, and push your finger inside, and probe the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the string, release it and push the intestine back into the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find a boil, they take it at the base, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery is doing the opposite, or the vein, go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and thread them with two strong threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done in the shape of a cross, as though you were piercing;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then draw the abscess in four places around the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles and let it drain until it can no longer, and push out the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is thin and flowing, then clean the abscess as necessary, and close the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the area as it should be, and bind the wound.
dou chancre	from cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the similarities of cancer, and how one should work with medicine, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and they say that ancient people believed that when cancer is in a place where one can scrape it, like cancer which is in breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one must completely remove it when it is in its beginning stages. And when it is old and large, one should not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatments, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then let them fester if there is a sign of fullness, then open the wound . Then cut off the cancer, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out freely, and squeeze the wound with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding from the artery or vein makes you feel uncomfortable, cauterize it until the blood vessels are closed; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
