Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already spoken of the appearances of dropsy and how the gathering of fluid occurs in each appearance, and its cure by means of medicine and also by the use of iron; therefore we will only briefly mention it here. And one should not use iron on these two appearances: that is, tympany and hydropsy, for they are deadly. So when you treat this type of dropsy called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not help, then one should look to see if the patient is weak or has any other illness besides dropsy, such as dysentery or similar conditions; in that case, do not use iron, for there is a risk involved. But if you see that the patient is strong and has no other illness besides dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed as follows:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Examine the patient's abdomen and press it gently with your hands to force the fluid towards the lowest part of the abdomen near the groin. Then take a spatumile (a type of needle used for bleeding) that is curved like a hook: it should be about two inches long but not so sharp that it punctures the intestines when inserted, nor so blunt that it does not Bleed the patient.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then determine if the dropsy is located near the intestines: in that case, you should make three small incisions on the right side of the abdomen below the navel. If the dropsy is due to a disease of the liver, then the incisions should be made on the left side, and if it is due to the spleen, they should be made on the right. The patient should not lie directly on top of the incisions so that the fluid does not flow into that weak area.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce all the skin with the instrument and insert it, and take your hand off the spatulum between the skin and the syringe as if you were skinning to the depth of a fingernail or nail; then pierce the syringe so that the spatulum comes to the desired location, which is where the water will go, then pull out the instrument, and insert this instrument from which there is the shape: And it resembles a thin silver rod, and it is made of brass or light bronze, and has in the lower part a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and it is the shape of the incision from which the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	at the top of which is the handle, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it will be drawn up onto the instrument immediately; therefore empty half or a third, because if you empty more than is appropriate in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the shock of the tool, or he will faint, or he will come close to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of his strength signify, and his pulse; then pull out the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the stopper in the hole on the syringe, about which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then resume the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw off a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this for a few days and avoid following it with food until only a little water remains in the stomach. And if you doubt the disease, leave a lot of water, the heat of the grave or sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if you dye from drinking; and with medicines that dry out until he is healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without an opening on the penis, or the opening is small and out of place. In this case, one should immediately pierce it with a very thin needle according to the following procedure: then put into the opening a very thin plug made of lead, and tie it and leave it for three or four days. And when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then replace the plug; and sometimes none is needed at all, because the urine that comes out does not allow it to close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those with a small opening will be cured by the lead plug as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its place are infected, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then the head of the penis and foreskin are cut to the size of a feather, so that the incision is in the middle, as it should be; and you must guard against bleeding which often occurs, and if it does, then stanch it with something that stanches blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters come on the penis, and they have an unseemly appearance; and there are harmful ones and harmless ones; so you must take them with a very sharp knife, cut them and clean them all out, then put on wet cotton with Egyptian ointment; then cure it with thin ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blister is malignant, with pus and discharge, then you must apply cautery to it. When you have cut it, and if the blister is on the shaft of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must first remove the blister that is inside; and when it is sutured, then cure the outside. For if you cure them both together, the skin of the penis will not be secure and might be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come into his penis and testicles; so you must cut away all that is black and corrupt, then apply the ointment of honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and vetch, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	If there is bleeding, administer the lunar cautery in the following manner: Cauteries have two functions together: that is, to stop bleeding and to prevent corruption. If the glans of the penis are damaged and retracted, you must insert a tube into the penis and let the patient urinate through it. And if the foreskin is inflamed at the tip of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised or due to an injury or abscess, then you must make an incision with a sharp instrument, so that the membrane is cut, and the foreskin is freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a difficult thing to cure, you must make an incision with a sharp instrument at the tip of the penis and under the foreskin; then gently open it and put a thin piece of wet linen in cold water so that it does not inflame again.
de la circoncision	on circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a matter of continuous dissection like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this act intentionally and properly on infants, it is necessary for us to do the best and most gentle job for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who made circumcisions all around, and on many occasions, and on a single newborn; the foreskin would then heal because there were two membranes, and sometimes one would be cut above and the other remained beneath.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they recover by covering, and the pain is doubled, and with the cleaning which is done on the penis is not secure the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the nail sometimes the iron slips, and ruins the work, and many times are born so that they do not need to be cleaned and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleaning that is done on the scrotum, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the testicles are cut justly above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, you cut it evenly all around; but the thread must be tied tightly around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that if you do it, you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the wand, and then you make him move in every way you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then hold it straight between your hands, and tie the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then blow on the skin, and draw the wand up until the head of the wand is in; then clean it well from the dirt that has accumulated there, then tie the place marked with a double thread, then tie it under one to another string; and hold it for two days by the second ligature at the wrist and the index finger, and press between the two ligatures, then lift the skin rapidly and draw out the head of the wand.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the blood run little by little, for it is the mucous membrane; and put powder on top of the powder a glue-soaked cloth from a hard-boiled egg, cooked in rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the mouthing is as follows: both sides are to be thin and sharp, and the ears should be as big as the palm of the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of the purification is when the pus within the incision has dried up; therefore you must extend it with your fingernail so that the wound forms an abscess; and scrape it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tweezers and scrape it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for 3 days, and that which is under the foreskin is swollen, then let it be until the abscesses are calm and the skin is lightly scraped; then scrape it as much as you can, and beware of the part of the foreskin, it will not harm him in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore treat the area of the wound with powdered medicine, as we have said in the treatise on powders; and if one scrapes too much from the core, and it goes upward, it will not harm him; therefore cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, or bowels, or dead fetus, or similar things that we have described in the previous section.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine is not released and you see that it is being retained by a stone lodged in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over at the knees with their feet placed on their back, pressing their stomach down from above the back, and holding their breath as hard as they can. This will cause the neck of the bladder to be compressed from above, forcing the stone out and allowing the urine to flow.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If the urine is still not released and the patient experiences great pain as we have described, then you must perform an extraction using a instrument called a 'syringe'. It should be made of thin, lightweight silver, with the shape of a bird's feather; the cannula should be about a palm and a half in length, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of releasing the urine is to take a double thread and tie a small piece of wool or cotton at the end, then insert the tip of the thread into the syringe. Coat the excess wool with oil or butter and push it all the way into the syringe. Then anoint the patient's bladder and penis with moist oil or olive oil and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the scrotum; then fill the syringe up to the bladder, and the patient will feel the pain go all the way to the empty spot, and if this is not done according to this order, because the person who guides it to where it needs to go is wrong; then tie the thread to all the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and use the syringe again until the bladder is emptied and the pain is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is accumulated there, and you see it oozing out with water and medicine, then do everything using the instrument called "clepsydra", and that is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see; the local hair should be shaved so that the medicine can take effect and stop the moisture, and pushed in when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see your medicines enter the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it out as it goes in; then push the catheter firmly in, and the moisture will enter the bladder, and the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	This is the form of the subtle enema used to cleanse the bladder: take a small gut and make a small noose at one end, and a larger one at the other;
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher up; and below there is a knot or the string splits; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the medicine with which you want to cleanse the bladder; then tie it between the two knots formed from a length of thin double thread, and heat one end of the medicine over the fire; then insert the tip of the catheter into the urethra, and hold your hand over the bladder to gently push all the medicine in, until the patient feels that the medicine has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it into .i. circle, and pierce it evenly all around; then thread .i. strong wire through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles .i. cloak, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, squeezing by hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in the division of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the testicles, and all the signs, and which type of stone one must work on in surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder occurs most often in children, and it is a sign that the urine flows from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hairy, and causes pain to the patient, and they can urinate many times, and then they become constipated; and many of these have a hernia; and the healing is much easier in children until they are 4 years old, and it is much more serious in the elderly, and it is in between youth and old age, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is much easier in those who have large stones than in those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema to draw out all the feces which is in the intestines. For it sometimes clogs up when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move him around so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out from above; then let him sit between your apparatus-clad hands, and his hands be underneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely tilted downward; then search for and touch the stone inside it;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	if you feel the stone in the cavity, then quickly cut into the stone. And if it does not come out with just touching, then wet your left index finger with oil, if the patient is an adult, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young teenager; and insert it into their rectum, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it up toward the neck of the bladder; then press with your finger and push it out to where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct the patient to extend his testicles upward with his right hand, and with his left hand pull back the skin underneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatulum, which has a curved shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And they cut between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel; and it should be straight on top of the stone, and both fingers should be on the anus, and the incision should be diagonal so that it is wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too big.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Sometimes the press with the fingers on the anus will cause the stone to come out without any effort; and you will know that there is a stone with angles and edges when it is painful to urinate; and sometimes there is one below, resembling a grape or a round pebble, which is easier to pass.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For one with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must squeeze with tweezers that are as sharp as a knife at the tip to squeeze the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert underneath a very thin instrument bent at the end; and if you cannot grab it like this, you widen the opening a little and if the blood comes out, you stop it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, insert the largest first into the neck of the bladder, then push it up, then pull it out, and then the smaller ones afterwards. And if it is very large, you must split it and make a larger incision. For two things can happen to the patient: they may die, or the urine may come out through an opening where the skin cannot heal; but nevertheless, try to pull it out, or break it with tweezers, until you have pulled it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and place on top of it a damp cloth steeped in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then resound the patient's chest, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, wash the site well with oil and water, then treat the wound with thin ointment and thick ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses and scorchings and congealing of blood in the bladder occur, and as a result the urine is held back in such a way that it cannot pass out with the urine: then insert your finger into the wound and draw out that blood, for if any remains, it will corrupt the bladder and burst it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and assist it in every way you know how until it is healed; and you ought to bind the two thighs together with bandages, and apply remedies to the site every hour.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; then the treatment of what I say above, that you should cut it many times, is an excuse for not cutting it. I have already experienced this myself.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this shape and let it be spiked at three angles on a poker:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone so that it cannot return to the bladder; then push the poker into the urethra gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the poker in your hand within the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then the urine will come at once, and press your hand on what is left of the stone inside the urethra. The stone will be broken at once and will come out with the urine, and the patient is healed;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason, tie a thread under the stone and another above it, then cut the urethra between the two threads, then pull the stone out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It sometimes happens that a stone becomes lodged in a woman's body, and if it does, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that the woman might be a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who will submit to examination, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third reason is that one cannot find a skilled woman who knows how to treat this disease with her hands; and the fourth reason is that a woman's stone is often deeper than a man's, which requires a deeper incision, and great fear is associated with it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if it is necessary to do so, one should take a wise midwife and cut it out with a knife, and if you cannot find such a midwife, then take a subtle and skilled male doctor who specializes in the treatment of women, and command him to do what you command regarding the inquiry into the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look very carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: then she should press her thumb against her vagina and feel for the stone; and if she finds it, she should hold it there under her thumb, and he should tell her to press her left hand firmly against her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she feels it, then she should move it slowly from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; then press on the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the anus, where it is most sensitive, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her thumb above or below the stone, and let the incision be very small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then push the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone so as to widen the wound enough for the stone to come out; and know that there are many types of stones: some are small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and have different textures. You should know their likenesses in order to identify them.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood does not stop, then apply powdered vitriol and hold it in place for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task, until the stone is removed, and have assistants who I told you about earlier to help you with your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood vessels burst and it is the artery that is cut, then put the powder on the spot and constrict with bandages and strips, and don't re-open it, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, lest the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the swelling has gone down, return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous membrane is nothing else than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is found under the heart of the testicles, and which contains the egg; and it is called "pus", and sometimes it is properly located in the membrane of the egg, if one believes that it is another egg; and what happens is not known for certain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this disease is due to weakness that comes from the testicles, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture takes many forms: sometimes it is a yellow colour, sometimes red, sometimes black, sometimes watery white, and there are many more variations.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this condition, for if it is in the white syphilis that we have described, there are red spots, .i. a little long like the shape of an egg, and it does not affect the testicles, because there is moisture all around them.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the scrotum itself, then it is a different type of abscess with part of an egg, and because of this one might think it is another kind of abscess;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sac, he feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test it with all the instruments whose form has been described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, which comes after the instrument, judge what is inside.

puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the scrotum with a sharp instrument through a large opening, and draw out all the water, and then put in your fingers, and let the scrotum return to its place; and do not touch the testicles, but only the scrotum; cut gently all around it in pieces, for if you do not cut it well and bleeding ensues, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the testicle has fallen out due to your action, then return it to its place when you have finished the work on the scrotum; then sew together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a single stitch, then treat it like any other wound until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another disease, then you must tie off the vessels that are suspended, fearing a rupture of blood; then cut open the scrotum all around the suspenders, extract the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if pus has gathered in two places together, know that these are two abscesses; then open the other part as you did the first, equally, then wash the blood away and put on soft poultice moistened with rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put another poultice moistened with wine and oil, and place over the two abscesses, and put on top of these doubled linen cloths, and tie it around all the joint according to this form:

et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this method of cauterization is used instead of an iron brand, and you must press a thin knife gently against the skin of the abscesses, and it should be heated as we have said, so that the white pus containing fluid is exposed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if he takes the cautery according to this form, and pierces that sinus deeply, and burns it with this subtle hot cautery:

et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if anything contrary happens, such as a hot abscess or blood flow, or anything else, then treat what is contrary to you according to what has already been said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, because of which it seems better to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come in the body, especially in the testes; and it is due to various causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known to be due to an excess of bitterness and fever, which are spread to the testes, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess follows the color of the body; and it does not hurt, and the abscess is serious;

Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a vein, it is recognized by the hot feeling of the abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	Those who are affected by inflammation of the veins are known by their appearance, through the sensation of touch with the fingers,
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and anyone can accurately make a diagnosis based on this examination and on other characteristics.

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the lymph nodes, or within the blood vessels, then you must deliver all of that tissue and cut it out cleanly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the tumor is in the back, then you must cut it out entirely and extract the egg, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the testicle abscess

de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the eye socket

puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then dress the wound with another ointment until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this section, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as the section that is together with the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting above and below lightly.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then press gently, and cure the abscess of him who opens it, until the vessels leak; and cure it as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the veins, as we have said, and the place opens up; and none of the intestines come out into the rectum, and if any do, it is rare, and repair it every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if he stays too long in this position, the wound or ulcer will close up, so that the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the ulcer, which is in the intestines, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen at its base and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then apply the poultice of the wound according to its size, according to the quantity of 3 pounds;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the cyst which is under the skin, then take a thread and place it over the visible location of the cyst;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	press it deeply into the belly, then tie the two ends of the thread appearing over the cyst on top of the thread, and tie one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull on the end of the thread, and do not cover the cyst or stretch it out with anything else, as I have told you in the treatment for a hernia of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with a wound treatment. And when you tie off the threads, if it is cleansed and treated, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ulcer is constrained and has no appearance in the roux, and cautery is more beneficial in this case and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles becomes soft in some men due to the organs within becoming softened, and it is milky white in appearance; and when one wishes to treat this, he must make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin above the natural membrane; then bring together the two edges of the wound at a single stitch, or at three or four stitches tightly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed, then remove the sutures.
dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You know that castration is condemned in our law, and because of this, I would rather not discuss it in this book. It is only necessary for two reasons: one is so that the owner knows how to respond when asked about it, and also knows how to treat it; the other is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as bulls, rams, and sheep. So I say that castration is done in two ways: by constriction or by cutting. For constriction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and hanging; then squeeze them in your hand until they are back in place and you can no longer feel them. For a cut castration: you must tie the animal down, press the skin of the testicles against your left hand, then make an incision, and cut each testicle open once as you have well-scalded them; leave some of the thinner sac and the fine membrane that is over the vessels; this method of castration is better than constriction, because with constriction something from the testicles may remain, causing the animal to desire sexual intercourse; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two types in terms of their appearance: one resembles a man but has the genitals and physical characteristics of a woman, sometimes even having body hair and urinating standing up. The other type appears as a woman but has a penis and testicles. For both types, you treat them like any other wound; for the second type, if the urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Testicles are a pair of organs located below the natural part, and they appear very ugly to look at; some women have them as large as a hand, and this is called the scrotum. You should cut off the excess of the testicles with your hand or with tweezers, and pluck it gently; do not pull too hard, or bleeding will occur, then cure the scrotum of another disease until it is healed; and there is another lump that grows at the mouth of the penis, and you should use it, and sometimes it pops out, and it looks like a cow's udder, and that is why the ancients called it the "cow disease". So you should pluck the testicles, as we have said, and cure them until they are healed.
de erratique	of the erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the opening of the woman's vagina is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to illness that came to her; or it is due to a growth, or a subtle or dense tumor, and it occurs deeply in the vagina, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and it hinders conception and childbirth, and sometimes flowers as well. The knowledge of this condition is through the examination of the vulva. If the growth is obvious, then you should examine it with your fingers or by sight. If it is a subtle tumor, and it is close to the two lips, then you should pull the lips together and hold them in place while the woman is lying on her back with her legs spread apart; then the lips will come together and cover the growth, and you should apply a poultice of wool soaked in oil over the area, and let the woman lie still for several days so that it does not heal. And if the tumor is hard and dense, then you should pluck it with tweezers similar to myrtle leaves. If the growth is due to a neonate, then you should pluck and apply a poultice; and use medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then apply a broad piece of linen so that the wound does not heal; and let it be for a long time, and apply a tent made of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed. And when a growth occurs in the vagina, you should treat it according to this method, if it is not an abscess. For in an abscess in the vagina, one should not touch it to treat it.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that normally bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed; and we have already discussed their appearances, signs, and treatment in a previous section. I stated that both hemorrhoids and thrombosed hemorrhoids, when they burst in the rectum, and do not bleed at all, cannot be cured by an iron cautery. Those that are near the edge of the anus can be felt and can be treated. Therefore, you should place the patient in a cool room, then cut off the blood supply to the hemorrhoids with ligatures, and burn their roots with a hot instrument; then powder the area with medicines that constrict blood vessels, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar substances; then she should soak her feet in cold water for an hour, then place her in a bath of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar ingredients; and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and garlic, and make an ointment to be applied to her back. If the bleeding stops, that is good. If not, she should use leeches on her back and breasts without using any instruments; then take wool and soak it in plantain juice or dogwood juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the affected area. And when the abscess has drained, treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough lump, so it should be cauterized as I have described for the thrombosed hemorrhoids; and then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the rectum
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that can occur in the rectum, such as ulcers, piercings, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, as well as several others that I have discussed earlier. Therefore, let me now describe the treatment for a hot abscess in the rectum, which is not among those that heal on their own; and if you want to know how to treat it with an instrument, observe whether the abscess is soft at the beginning of its appearance, and whether there is heat and fever, and if it turns red when you can see it. Then, do not rush to pierce it, but let it be lanced only after the pain has subsided; then have the patient sit on a seat with two small pillows to lean against, and support his back, and spread his legs apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them together with a good cord; then suck the anus towards the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the rectum, through which the abscess will drain; and you should insert the tip of the instrument first to determine the depth of the rectum so that the instrument does not go in too far or hurt the patient. If the instrument is larger, cover the opening of the rectum with cloth so that it does not cause discomfort to the patient; and you should hold the instrument in place with your thumb, and apply the instrument. When the abscess breaks open and the content is soft, then cover the wound at the opening of the rectum with a tent made of moist rosin or dried olive oil; and place the tent inside the rectum, pushing it deep into the rectum and against the wall of the rectum; then apply ointment after two days, as long as it is needed until the wound heals. Sometimes, raising the rectum and the wound with a syringe of water and honey helps; then use water in which roots of iris and aristolochia have been boiled; then return to using the ointment. If the wound has drained inside the rectum, then you should avoid cauterization with iron, but treat it as I have described earlier.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is first necessary for the midwife to understand the natural shape of childbirth and its signs: when you see a woman pushing downward and desiring to smell an aroma, then hasten the baby's exit; then you know that this childbirth follows nature's course, and the birth canal opens beneath her head, and the afterbirth emerges with it. And when you see these signs, gently press her abdomen so that the child is born quickly; for when the infant descends upon its head, the afterbirth follows, and the mother is cleansed of her excess fluids through proper purification; and those who are delivered otherwise are not born naturally. For sometimes a child is delivered upon its feet, or emerges from the body through the arms or abdomen, or comes out upside down, or in other unnatural positions; thus the midwife must be wise and subtle in these matters, guarding against error and deception, and I will show you all the forms and how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born naturally upon its head, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty and her strength wanes, then make her sit upon a stool or have women support her; and heat some olive oil or fried fenugreek, and then pour it between the midwife's fingers into the small opening of which there is now the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and split the afterbirth, and squeeze its nail until the fluids within flow out; and press upon the woman's abdomen so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then cleanse the woman's intestines with a poultice of fenugreek and olive oil; then make her sneeze and cough, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will be delivered. And if both hands emerge, then you must gently pull them back in little by little; and if they cannot enter, then have the woman sit upon a chair, and lift her feet upward; then raise the chair off the ground, and hold her so that she does not strain while standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then grip the hands at the knuckles as mentioned before, and extract the child, and reset the hands likewise.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	of the birth of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child is born standing up, it should be turned over;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn him slowly and gently until he is straight;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then grab one of his feet and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Let him jump up to his waist, if he can, and make him sneeze by sniffing something.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he can jump, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he cannot jump as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is in his natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he is easily cured.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take musk, and oil of vitriol, and melted gum, and grind them all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the nature of the woman inside and force this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then have her sit in warm water up to below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened underneath, make her a collar of myrrh and put it on her underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and constrict her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will jump out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	for the child to come out over his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this way, he puts his hands on the mother's belly gently.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then she lies down on her back, and the feet hang down, and she lies on her side;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bends her hands little by little, and then presses her hands on his belly, and lifts the cushions underneath so that she is ready to go down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then she takes her feet and moves them about, then she moves his belly upwards, then she puts your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and rocks the child gently; and instructs the woman to squeeze until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes out width a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	The patient's hand must be brought back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, have the woman stand up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, have her lie on a bed and raise her legs straight;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the medicine I mentioned earlier;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study to bring the hand back;
