puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should cut it bleeding to your power, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and it is healed deeply.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and where he feels it most;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for certain the location, whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you about, if the pain is according to what I have told you
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the filth and rotten flesh within
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is quite deep in a straight line, then you should open it as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply moist tenting to medicine the abscess, and I pack it up to the top of the fistula
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply warming ointments to the healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve causes you grief in your principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, then cut it until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cleanse it with warm water until it is clean;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and returns bent as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone to the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and desire as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way than to let it heal naturally;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can pull out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if he is extracted with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull them out one by one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it worse, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	cut and burn and scrape the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something on the wound to stop the bleeding.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it remain until the swelling goes down around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have more ease with the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you merely treat the corruption until all the darkness has been removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large amount of corruption, and it reaches the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	one must scrape and cover it all the way to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you can take example and help from your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the fluids came to his leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason for it to open;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but they miraculously worked so much that the abscesses opened
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter came out and it became a fistula, and many holes opened up all over the body from which pus and moisture flowed;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many were treated for more than two years, and no one in the art of medicine had any success,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called to see him, and saw his leg and the remedies they were using to treat it,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which ran through the holes of the body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the bodies of the young men, and had yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent at one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried therefore, and struck one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came right up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be rotten bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then begin again, and expose the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then I had to work hard to solder the area;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't do anything until I copied around one palm of bone, and the trauma affected all his body;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I healed him with medicine; and he was cured and healed very quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it is not necessary to repeat the operation except for the weakness of the patient who cannot endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of my fear of his death that I had.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For despite the bloodletting, he often bled but was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there grew up in the place of the bone hard flesh, and he was of good constitution and had no harm nor evil in any way, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set as follows:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a thread and wind it around the head of the bone which protrudes,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and have someone pull it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another thicker thread of woolen cloth over the bone that is dislocated,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and are the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh from below,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the place where you see it is sore, so that the thread does not cut the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot iron or a table underneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must sew as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and sew again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is broken but does not open, and the fracture is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the flesh completely; then place a hot iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then sew up from one end of the fracture to the other, as we have said, and let the sewing be done from the length of the fracture with a needle,
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the fracture is in the joint, then cut through the joint, and sew up the bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut it off;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the wrist of the foot, then that thing is very strong,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless you must examine this corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful not to damage the vein or nerve;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and you shall know that the incisions and sutures for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the orifices.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and thinness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason one should prepare a different instrument for each kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And you shall know that the work will show you the instrument which you need according to your knowledge of this craft,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and bear witness to the ways of sickness;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	prepare the instrument that you need according to what is appropriate for it.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may dislocate due to internal or external causes;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated this corrosion with remedies, but they do not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then cover the limb up to the site of the corrosion,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes through the air or through evil, which is greater, due to the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after darkness, then goes the corrosion of members from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes over the whole body; so be quick about covering it up,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's caused by the sting of some venomous creatures, like scorpions and vipers, or similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head or neck, then cover it up and do not leave any gaps for the poison to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, then apply the cautery to the joint so that the corrosion does not go up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, then apply the cautery to the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy for its strength except according to the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus it is done when the cautery comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then apply the cautery after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it occurs on the foot, cut off the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it climbs up the leg, cut off at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to kill the patient with a knife;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the method of cutting on the leg or arm is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one minister extends one of the strings downstream, and another minister extends the other string upstream,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the rope that is between the two strings to a width of one spatium, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the thread or silk, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the silk does not touch the healthy area,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and cause another injury and abscess in the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood comes out when you operate, then cauterize the area gently.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the dislocated member with an appropriate bandage and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a man with a similar injury:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a darkness which looked like a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his toe of the foot, so that it affected all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he stopped bleeding and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corrosion returned to his finger on the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied impact poultices after cleansing the body, but could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he requested that I cup his hand, and I did not want to until I had hope of removing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, that he would not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and healed his hand.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have told you this tale only so that someone else may benefit from it if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes great swelling;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rupture and discharge, and the place remains hollow, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above is as delicate as a loose napkin,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called  "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches to the bone inside, then it is called   "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is to apply a cautery around it all, especially when it is subtle, just like a napkin.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not worry about its destruction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are concerned that the skin will burn, and the destruction is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then the cure is thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are swollen, and the bowels within are of foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	therefore use an egyptian medicated clyster made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafoetida, and oil, and litharge, equally, and mix and cook in a vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take as much as you need, and mix it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and insert it into the breast, and constrict the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medication in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this as many times as necessary until the breast is relieved and the pore is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are cauterized with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you burn vine wood ashes, and pour water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it run, and cauterize with it as much as you know the wound is open;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine, nor the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if one enemas with water and honey, or a little litarge ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can use enema of honey and wine, as honey has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes one sweat.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this, and you are sure that the chest is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if he enemas with what makes him defecate
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you press the ointment of diafinit, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you enema with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have discussed in the section on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the anus is small, and the rectum of the enema cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if one widens it with an iron a little, and puts in some of the Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then cut and leave only enough room for the syringe to enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening that the bowels hang out of is at the top, then the cut should be made below where they are.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is fully drawn, do not allow the string to snap.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	arrange it so that the bow runs to the lowest place it can reach,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bow is fully drawn, do not allow the string to snap
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	you should dress it in this way: let the bow run smoothly downward, and leave nothing of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and they are on a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then press as hard as you can on the opening of the armpit; make the second hole larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft ointment over another small piece of cloth according to the size of the hole,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the armpit opening to ease the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth for several days;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one who is above the armpit opening, remove often to remove the bowstring,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what flows from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digestive fluid, or indigestion;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	take care if the patient feels pain or not, and see if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when the medicine has spread in such a way, and you see the nature that pops out of the opening of the breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is firm, and approach the saint;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning, or at midday, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change a different cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows low and indigestible after many days, know that the breast does not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom flows after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is nearby. For there are men who apply delayed treatments to their wounds, and others who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if milk is not digested and rises from the breast after many days, know that the breasts will not open;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are delayed in opening and are distant, then apply dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in effect,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	like diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and it is the best medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a definite ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and rose wine of equal substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then cook it and use it; and with the same honey cooked, thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when a definite ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey while it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then in glue a cloth, and they put it over the breast, and sometimes they administer a long aristolache.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of heavenly lily, which is like flour of wheat and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and the use of simples or compounds: grind them to powder and place on the honey I mentioned earlier and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then you know that the corruption is complete, and it makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard members, or in the soft tissues;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if there is an abscess under a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that develops under the fingernail on the finger of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from the foot, or perhaps from other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes infected and one takes no care, then an abscess forms,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and ooze pus as long as they run to the root of the nail, and perhaps they run all the way;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion comes to the bone, as long as there is a foul-smelling pain, and the finger is swollen, and the colour is green.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess material that is underneath the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to push out and break the skin,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should put a thread under the nail so that it doesn't cut into the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and draw it out on top, and carefully and gently split the skin,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the inflammation until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decaying, pull it out with a pair of tongs as previously described,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the inflammation until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must treat it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the big toe diagonally from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cutter does not go all the way to the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	You must adjust the two joints which sometimes grow in men's hands by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone, and sometimes only bone, and sometimes only nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some grow at the root of the joint, where the growth is in some of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a hernia in any part of his body does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the junction of the neck, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of one who is fleshy is slight in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; if you hold it tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born in the anus, you should first cut around the flesh roundly to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone to a suitable depth, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by joint wound, or by burn from fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Then you must treat this wound so that it heals according to its natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	place between two pieces of damp cloth or gauze soaked in rose oil so that it does not seal.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you can place them between two pieces of thin linen, as long as the wound seals, as it should.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sealing occurs on one of his hands with the palm, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
Des vils	Of the base
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Viles are large veins wrapped in a fullness of melancholy superfluities, which come to many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more occurs in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a cleansing enema, and then the basilicon ointment.Et li amonestre et la maniere dou saine et dou cautere, et que il doit faire, si te veult dire.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with fire has two methods: one is to use cupping glasses, drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The treatment for lacerations is as follows: first, cut the leg with very hot water, until the large veins are made slender,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient from above the thigh to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	and squeeze and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the nature of the disease can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to use a poultice of black gall-nut;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the bloodletting and purging again when the veins are empty, according to the disease.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatments for this condition are as follows: shave the leg of the patient if there is a lot of hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it with fire, and then press it from the top of the knee to the bottom of the ankle, or in the area below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scorch the vein from each side, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it resembles a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pierce the vein below, so that it is raised from the skin, and then it can be bound gently
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut into the vein in another place above, twice; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up by the vein, as you did before, and bind it at another uncine, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another nail, or several if you need them, then lift it, and strike the bottom of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull and lift up to the second nail; then pull it out nail by nail, until it comes out completely, then strike it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then thread a strong double piece of wire through it,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it out, and put a needle under the nail, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be sure it does not pop, for if it pops, one cannot milk or lift it, and this causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished milking it, place a pad soaked in wine and rosemary oil over the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the nerve is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must split it torturedly, but do not pop it; and milk it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not cut unless it touches the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	It has a thick curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but it should be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein:
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in hot areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture:
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it occurs elsewhere than on the legs, and this happens due to the pustules that form under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as happens with serpents and worms that live between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this illness are that there is a great swelling in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the colour changes, and the illness starts to come out, just as from the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, you must wrap it with a piece of lead from one and a half to two inches, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the lead hang down to the leg, and every time it is not in place, wrap it around the lead again, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a portion, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at the root until it is fully dislocated;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cover it, it will go into the flesh, causing abscess and swelling in that place, and great illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	this thing must be treated little by little until it reaches the head, and nothing is left in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein, when treated with five or ten palm-widths,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it issued ten palm-widths long; and when you grab it, it pushes out a finger's width or an opening, and it penetrates to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and after emptying the matter inside, bring medicine to the site in a gently oozing manner for several days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein is found to be raining, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out of a hole and rains down; therefore treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often affects oxen:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm that rises between skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending;
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it moves from one member to another, until it finds an opening in the skin, and then it jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by the putrefaction of some humours, like worms and serpents and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is concern about its malice, for when it moves through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and milked, one cannot help but feel compassion when he sees it:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong string, tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then press on it from above and milk it firmly, and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you do not bring it out,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire on top, as long as it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, grip under the eyelid firmly, then pull upwards and out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one must use a cleansing ointment for the body made from digestive medicines to draw out the bad humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there is swelling from rotten flesh.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, who uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise as high as a worm at her shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than anything else, just like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place and moved to her shoulder,The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then soon spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he would tell me that she was turning around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease progress in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want to, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because women had dry bodies and exposed veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of that they appear to have constricted wind.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	But it does not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels pain as we have said, if it appears to you
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	[if] the fluid above and below is pus, and then press on [it] until that constrained pus comes out;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment of those who draw out pus, like putrid pills and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their tips is that there are some with large points, small points, threaded, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	There are also arrows with two angles, those with heads, and those with pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and it is removed from any joint of its place, according to which it cannot move, and the limb is deformed, and suffers great pain and injury.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore occurs in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you should be careful about extracting this arrow, because death comes afterward in various ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not disappear, and the arrow is not completely removed, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the blood flows from above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a cutting and piercing of the head and brain, and blood flows from the wound and there is inflammation and redness in the face and tongue, and spasms and confusion in the mind, and vomiting of blood;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes blood flows from the nose or ears; and sometimes they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes white moisture resembling pus, and it seeps out like a boil;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, cease the treatment and remove the arrow if it is in there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it is on the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were pierced into a hard object, not open.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the wound also becomes mute like the pulse, and short black blood comes out, and there is chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	you know without a doubt that death will come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that affects the lung is spitting foam from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the foot, it affects the small bones; and there is great pain and swelling and discomfort, and the patient feels pain throughout their shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out through the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the intestines in the abdomen, and no feces escape through the rear end, then there is no hope for a cure or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows outward, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There once was a man who was shot with an arrow in the jaw at its root near the teeth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it and extracted it from below the ear fat, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that shot him in the oil fat under the paper under,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was replanted, and he could not reach it except for the tip towards the forest,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large, shot from a Turkish bow, entering just behind the ears; the boy remained unharmed and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he took an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow that had entered behind his ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut away the barbs, and extracted it carefully, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he took an arrow that had pierced a man's throat, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then if he has not improved after .xxx. days,
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and experienced no ill effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow wound in his back, and the wound is closed over:
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions do not change,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	one will not find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow hit him in the face and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I saw an arrow hit a noble man of the king's court, whom the arrow had entered the eye,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was somewhat declined to the right side; and the arrow was all drawn out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to tend the wound after she had given birth .iiij. days later. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it everywhere with my fingers and could not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt stabbing and pain underneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of an arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the place a soothing and digestive plaster, so that the swelling would go down.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the tip of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for a longer time, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was healed
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed the wound and felt the tip of the arrowhead inside;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied the corrosive medicine to the wound until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and transgress well the terms around 4 months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then lacerate if the wound that I pricked with tweezers and probed from one side to another, but could not get out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not cease to subtilize and devise means of instruments, until I took it on the .i. day with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will come in the end of this chapter, as far as I drew it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they who know this judge that cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I therefore restored it; and the wound was sewed up, and the patient entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I will tell you about extracting certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may apply your treatment to what I have not mentioned, for the books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters consider well very little, and what is present and lacking to them,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works, and new instruments, and the descent of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are stuck according to .ij. ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and if it jumps out of its place, it is an arrow entering the flesh, and sometimes it will jump out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, leave it as long as the wound around it becomes pus-filled and the exit is cleared.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for a few days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it doesn't, then pierce around it with a very thin needle to widen the exit, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent to the patient; then do not extract it, but let it be until it is even with the skin after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes as far as the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not lodged in the bone, and does not come as far as the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without a bad turn, if the device to draw is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very swollen and cannot come out, then administer blisters around it, as I have told you; then clean the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body so that it cannot be seen, then one should search for it throughout the entire body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	then there is no bone or nerve or vein, as long as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut away the flesh that is stuck to it in the .ii parts that you can reach,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold the ears of the arrow so that you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot on one try, then leave it until the wound around it is swollen; then pull it out, for extraction is eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you doubtful, then follow what we have said about the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and opening a vein, and use whatever means you can to pull out the arrow without peril,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and adjust the patient according to how they were positioned when the arrow struck them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest aid you can provide; and if you cannot, then position them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another direction, where there is an opening or swelling on the skin, either visible or apparent to the touch:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut it off, then, as high up as the pincers can reach, and then pull it out; if not, jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand rapidly, forcing it into the bone and widening the opening; then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot be removed, leave it for now and try again later to extract it.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is an arrow shaft, push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if you see that it is swollen, and you want to apply a poultice, then you should apply .i. cold poultice,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the flesh of the instrument; and then draw it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is lodged deeply, apply 1 pointed instrument to ease its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around it where the venom is, as much as you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the buttock, or the thigh, belly, bladder, or side, and it is superficial, and you can cover it with a bandage, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, then extract the arrow, and then sew up the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to an owl's beak; see the diagram.
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the head of the forceps is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown in this diagram:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tongs for pushing and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one heals, there are 31, from which there are 16 in the head,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: 2 veins that are behind the ears, which are called the two "ear-veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are visible in each temple;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins which are found in the eyelids, called "aspiring."
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two gullets which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins which are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called 'augerich'.
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which comes from the left side, and the common people call it the 'vein of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle part is called the "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and common people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the pubic bone,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one they use for bleeding, which clearly opens above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the pulse is the vein that is between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two movements.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg there are three pulses: one is under the curve of the pocket on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second superficial pulse is located at the ankle of the right side; and the pulse called 'queen', which is located at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three pulses below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrh and by migration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the sanitor, as I told you, and it is that you heal the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's neck with a wet towel,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears, coming down from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	examine them with your fingers, and press down where you feel the pulse under your finger, then make an incision there.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancelet and pierce under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through both skin and vein well twice, and let blood flow until you see it.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind it up tightly, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is worth bleeding from ancient times,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sudatory and ophthalmy that are used, and the body of tears agues as themselves;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of bleeding as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse below your finger, and then sign inside;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lightly press on the vein above at your index finger, and insert the lance beneath,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lightly press the vein above, and pinch it, just as you did in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then ligature it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cause and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is just as effective for old diseases of the face, and for migraines and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient turns their neck while twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the tip on the vein and press with your hand or something else and let the blood flow according to the amount you want to see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then tie the vein so that it is healthy and sometimes the wound with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flames to be too sharp; and heal across, because the bone is close by, and perhaps break the flames when they are fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two layers, which help each other, and in the eye, and in facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the nature of their healing is that the patient twists his neck while pulling on a thread, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then he heals, and the healing is through the tongue, a little from the long flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they will break; then draw blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for epilepsy, and sudden madness, and illnesses of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient should squeeze his neck, then press his nose with his left hand,
